Wait, when computing E(S1·S2), it's the expectation value over the state ψ, which is a symmetric combination of |↑↑↓⟩, |↑↓↑⟩, and |↓↑↑⟩.

So, each term in ψ has two up spins and one down spin, but in different positions.

So, for S1·S2:

- In |↑↑↓⟩, S1 and S2 are both up, so positive contribution.
- In |↑↓↑⟩, S1 is up and S2 is down, so negative contribution.
- In |↓↑↑⟩, S1 is down and S2 is up, so negative contribution.

So, each of the three terms contributes either +1/4 ħ², -1/4 ħ², or -1/4 ħ².

Since ψ is a symmetric combination, each term occurs with equal weight.

Therefore, E(S1·S2) = (1/3)( (1/4) + (-1/4) + (-1/4) ) ħ² = (1/3)( -1/4 ) ħ² = -1/12 ħ².

Similarly, let's compute E(S1·S3):

In |↑↑↓⟩, S1 is up, S3 is down: negative contribution, so -1/4 ħ².
In |↑↓↑⟩, S1 is up, S3 is up: positive, +1/4 ħ².
In |↓↑↑⟩, S1 is down, S3 is up: negative, -1/4 ħ².

So, E(S1·S3) = (1/3)( (-1/4) + (1/4) + (-1/4) ) ħ² = (1/3)( (-1/4) ) ħ² = -1/12 ħ².

Similarly, compute E(S2·S3):

In |↑↑↓⟩, S2 is up, S3 is down: negative, -1/4 ħ².
In |↑↓↑⟩, S2 is down, S3 is up: negative, -1/4 ħ².
In |↓↑↑⟩, S2 is up, S3 is up: positive, +1/4 ħ².

- <σ1_x σ2_x> = 0
- <σ1_y σ2_y> = 0

Wait, that seems complicated, but maybe manageable.

First, let me note that (S1 + S2)^2 = S1² + S2² + 2 S1·S2.

We already know ⟨S1²⟩ = ⟨S2²⟩ = (3/4) ħ².

Wait, let's write out (S1 + S2)^2 in terms of Pauli matrices.

For spin-1/2 particles, S_i can be represented as (ħ/2) σ_i, where σ_i are the Pauli matrices.

So, S1 + S2 = (ħ/2)(σ1 + σ2). Then, (S1 + S2)^2 = (ħ²/4)(σ1 + σ2)² = (ħ²/4)(σ1² + σ2² + 2 σ1·σ2).

Since σ1² = I, the identity matrix, and similarly for σ2². So, σ1 + σ2 squared is σ1² + σ2² + 2 σ1·σ2.

Therefore, (S1 + S2)^2 = (ħ²/4)(I + I + 2 σ1·σ2) = (ħ²/4)(2I + 2 σ1·σ2) = (ħ²/2)(I + σ1·σ2).

Wait, so (S1 + S2)^2 = (ħ²/2)(I + σ1·σ2).

Therefore, ⟨(S1 + S2)^2⟩ = (ħ²/2) ⟨I + σ1·σ2⟩.

Since I is identity, ⟨I⟩ is 1. So, ⟨(S1 + S2)^2⟩ = (ħ²/2)(1 + ⟨σ1·σ2⟩).

Thus, ⟨σ1·σ2⟩ = ⟨(S1 + S2)^2⟩ - (ħ²/2).

But ⟨σ1·σ2⟩ can be calculated because σ1·σ2 = 2 S1·S2, as S_i = (ħ/2) σ_i.

Wait, indeed, S1·S2 = (ħ²/4) σ1·σ2.

So, ⟨S1·S2⟩ = (ħ²/4) ⟨σ1·σ2⟩.

Therefore, now, let's compute ⟨σ1·σ2⟩ for the state ψ.

σ1·σ2 = σ1^x σ2^x + σ1^y σ2^y + σ1^z σ2^z.

So, ⟨σ1·σ2⟩ = ⟨ψ| σ1^x σ2^x |ψ⟩ + ⟨ψ| σ1^y σ2^y |ψ⟩ + ⟨ψ| σ1^z σ2^z |ψ⟩.

So, let's compute each of these terms.

First, let's compute ⟨ψ| σ1^z σ2^z |ψ⟩.

Since σ1^z |↑⟩ = +1 |↑⟩, σ1^z |↓⟩ = -1 |↓⟩.

So, σ1^z σ2^z |↑₁↑₂↓₃⟩ = (1)(1) |↑₁↑₂↓₃⟩ = |↑₁↑₂↓₃⟩.

Similarly, σ1^z σ2^z |↑₁↓₂↑₃⟩ = (1)(-1) |↑₁↓₂↑₃⟩ = -|↑₁↓₂↑₃⟩.

Similarly, σ1^z σ2^z |↓₁↑₂↑₃⟩ = (-1)(1) |↓₁↑₂↑₃⟩ = -|↓₁↑₂↑₃⟩.

Therefore, ⟨ψ| σ1^z σ2^z |ψ⟩ = (1/3)[⟨↑₁↑₂↓₃|↑₁↑₂↓₃⟩ - ⟨↑₁↓₂↑₃|↑₁↓₂↑₃⟩ - ⟨↓₁↑₂↑₃|↓₁↑₂↑₃⟩ ].

Which is (1/3)[1 - 1 -1] = (1/3)(-1) = -1/3.

So, ⟨ψ| σ1^z σ2^z |ψ⟩ = -1/3.

Next, compute ⟨ψ| σ1^x σ2^x |ψ⟩ and ⟨ψ| σ1^y σ2^y |ψ⟩.

Hmm, σ^x and σ^y are more complicated because they are raising and lowering operators.

For σ1^x σ2^x, acting on the state |↑₁↑₂↓₃⟩.

σ1^x |↑⟩ = |↓⟩, σ2^x |↑⟩ = |↓⟩.

So, σ1^x σ2^x |↑₁↑₂↓₃⟩ = |↓₁↓₂↑₃⟩.

Similarly, σ1^x σ2^x |↑₁↓₂↑₃⟩ = |↓₁↑₂↓₃⟩.

And σ1^x σ2^x |↓₁↑₂↑₃⟩ = |↑₁↓₂↑₃⟩.

Therefore, when we apply σ1^x σ2^x to each term in ψ, we get:

σ1^x σ2^x |↑₁↑₂↓₃⟩ = |↓₁↓₂↑₃⟩,

σ1^x σ2^x |↑₁↓₂↑₃⟩ = |↓₁↑₂↓₃⟩,

σ1^x σ2^x |↓₁↑₂↑₃⟩ = |↑₁↓₂↑₃⟩.

So, ⟨ψ| σ1^x σ2^x |ψ⟩ is (1/3) [⟨ψ| ↓₁↓₂↑₃⟩ + ⟨ψ| ↓₁↑₂↓₃⟩ + ⟨ψ| ↑₁↓₂↑₃⟩ ].

⟨↑₁↓₂↑₃| ↓₁↓₂↑₃⟩ = 0,

⟨↓₁↑₂↑₃| ↓₁↓₂↑₃⟩ = 0.

So, ⟨ψ| ↓₁↓₂↑₃⟩ = 0.

Similarly, ⟨ψ| ↓₁↑₂↓₃⟩: compute (1/√3)(⟨↑₁↑₂↓₃| ↓₁↑₂↓₃⟩ + ⟨↑₁↓₂↑₃| ↓₁↑₂↓₃⟩ + ⟨↓₁↑₂↑₃| ↓₁↑₂↓₃⟩).

Each term:

⟨↑₁↑₂↓₃| ↓₁↑₂↓₃⟩ = 0,

⟨↑₁↓₂↑₃| ↓₁↑₂↓₃⟩ = 0,

⟨↓₁↑₂↑₃| ↓₁↑₂↓₃⟩ = 0.

So, ⟨ψ| ↓₁↑₂↓₃⟩ = 0.

⟨↓↑↑|↑↓⟩: first different, second different, third different: zero.

So, <ψ| S1^z S3^z |ψ> = (1/3)(⟨↑↑↓| + ⟨↑↓↑| + ⟨↓↑↑|) * (|↑↑↓⟩ + |↑↓↑⟩ + |↓↑↑⟩) evaluated at the z-components.

But let's compute it step by step.

For each term in |ψ⟩, compute S1^z S3^z |term⟩:

For |↑↑↓⟩:
S1^z |↑↑↓⟩ = (ħ/2)|↑↑↓⟩,
S3^z |↑↑↓⟩ = (-ħ/2)|↑↑↓⟩,
so S1^z S3^z |↑↑↓⟩ = (-ħ²/4)|↑↑↓⟩.

For |↑↓↑⟩:
S1^z |↑↓↑⟩ = (ħ/2)|↑↓↑⟩,
S3^z |↑↓↑⟩ = (ħ/2)|↑↓↑⟩,
so S1^z S3^z |↑↓↑⟩ = (ħ²/4)|↑↓↑⟩.

For |↓↑↑⟩:
S1^z |↓↑↑⟩ = (-ħ/2)|↓↑↑⟩,
S3^z |↓↑↑⟩ = (ħ/2)|↓↑↑⟩,
so S1^z S3^z |↓↑↑⟩ = (-ħ²/4)|↓↑↑⟩.

Therefore, S1^z S3^z |ψ⟩ = (1/√3)( (-1/4)|↑↑↓⟩ + (1/4)|↑↓↑⟩ + (-1/4)|↓↑↑⟩ ).

Now, <ψ| S1^z S3^z |ψ> = (1/√3)(⟨↑↑↓| + ⟨↑↓↑| + ⟨↓↑↑| ) * [ (-1/4)|↑↑↓⟩ + (1/4)|↑↓↑⟩ - (1/4)|↓↑↑⟩ ].

As before, only terms where the ket and bra are the same contribute. Let's check each:

⟨↑↑↓|↑↑↓⟩ = 1,
⟨↑↑↓|↑↓↑⟩ = 0,
⟨↑↑↓|↓↑↑⟩ = 0.

Similarly for others:

⟨↑↓↑|↑↑↓⟩ = 0,
⟨↑↓↑|↑↓↑⟩ = 1,
⟨↑↓↑|↓↑↑⟩ = 0.

⟨↓↑↑|↑↑↓⟩ = 0,
⟨↓↑↑|↑↓↑⟩ = 0,
⟨↓↑↑|↓↑↑⟩ = 1.

So, the only non-zero terms are:

⟨↑↑↓|↑↑↓⟩ * (-1/4) = (-1/4),
⟨↑↓↑|↑↓↑⟩ * (1/4) = 1/4,
⟨↓↑↑|↓↑↑⟩ * (-1/4) = (-1/4).

So, <ψ| S1^z S3^z |ψ> = (1/√3)( (-1/4) + (1/4) + (-1/4) ) = (1/√3)( (-1/4) ) = -1/(4√3) ħ².

Similarly, let's compute <S1^x S3^x> and <S1^y S3^y>.

Starting with <S1^x S3^x>:

The operator S1^x S3^x acting on each term:

For |↑↑↓⟩:
S1^+ S3^+ |↑↑↓⟩ = S1^+ |↑⟩ ⊗ S3^+ |↓⟩ = 0 ⊗ 0 = 0,
S1^+ S3^- |↑↑↓⟩ = 0 ⊗ |↑⟩ = 0,
S1^- S3^+ |↑↑↓⟩ = |↓⟩ ⊗ 0 = 0,
S1^- S3^- |↑↑↓⟩ = |↓⟩ ⊗ |↑⟩ = |↓↑⟩.

So, S1^x S3^x |↑↑↓⟩ = (0 + 0 + 0 + |↓↑⟩)/4, which is |↓↑⟩/4.

For |↑↓↑⟩:
S1^+ S3^+ |↑↓↑⟩ = 0 ⊗ 0 = 0,
S1^+ S3^- |↑↓↑⟩ = 0 ⊗ |↑⟩ = 0,
S1^- S3^+ |↑↓↑⟩ = |↓⟩ ⊗ |↑⟩ = |↓↑⟩,
S1^- S3^- |↑↓↑⟩ = |↓⟩ ⊗ |↓⟩ = |↓↓⟩.

So, S1^x S3^x |↑↓↑⟩ = (0 + 0 + |↓↑⟩ + |↓↓⟩)/4 = (|↓↑⟩ + |↓↓⟩)/4.

For |↓↑↑⟩:
S1^+ S3^+ |↓↑↑⟩ = |↑⟩ ⊗ |↓⟩ = |↑↓⟩,
S1^+ S3^- |↓↑↑⟩ = |↑⟩ ⊗ 0 = 0,
S1^- S3^+ |↓↑↑⟩ = 0 ⊗ |↓⟩ = 0,
S1^- S3^- |↓↑↑⟩ = 0 ⊗ 0 = 0.

So, S1^x S3^x |↓↑↑⟩ = (|↑↓⟩ + 0 + 0 + 0)/4 = |↑↓⟩/4.

Therefore, S1^x S3^x |ψ⟩ = (1/√3)( |↓↑⟩/4 + (|↓↑⟩ + |↓↓⟩)/4 + |↑↓⟩/4 ).

Simplify this:

= (1/√3) [ |↓↑⟩/4 + |↓↑⟩/4 + |↓↓⟩/4 + |↑↓⟩/4 ]

= (1/√3) [ (|↓↑⟩ + |↑↓⟩)/4 + |↓↓⟩/4 ]

So, <ψ| S1^x S3^x |ψ> = (1/√3)( ⟨↑↑↓| + ⟨↑↓↑| + ⟨↓↑↑| ) * [ (|↓↑⟩ + |↑↓⟩)/4 + |↓↓⟩/4 ]

= (1/√3) [ (⟨↑↑↓| + ⟨↑↓↑| + ⟨↓↑↑| ) |↓↑⟩ /4 + ⟨↑↑↓| |↓↓⟩ /4 + ⟨↑↓↑| |↓↓⟩ /4 + ⟨↓↑↑| |↓↓⟩ /4 ]

Now, evaluating each term:

⟨↑↑↓|↓↑⟩ = 0,
⟨↑↓↑|↓↑⟩ = 0,
⟨↓↑↑|↓↑⟩ = 1,
⟨↑↑↓|↓↓⟩ = 0,
⟨↑↓↑|↓↓⟩ = 0,
⟨↓↑↑|↓↓⟩ = 0.

Thus, only the term ⟨↓↑↑|↓↑⟩ contributes (1/4), so:

<ψ| S1^x S3^x |ψ> = (1/√3)( 1/4 ) = 1/(4√3) ħ².

Similarly, let's compute <S1^y S3^y>.

This would be quite involved, but let me try.

The operator S1^y S3^y = (S1^+ - S1^-)(S3^+ - S3^-)/(-4).

So, S1^y S3^y |↑↑↓⟩:

S1^+ S3^+ |↑↑↓⟩ = 0 ⊗ 0 = 0,
S1^+ S3^- |↑↑↓⟩ = 0 ⊗ |↑⟩ = 0,
S1^- S3^+ |↑↑↓⟩ = |↓⟩ ⊗ 0 = 0,
S1^- S3^- |↑↑↓⟩ = |↓⟩ ⊗ |↑⟩ = |↓↑⟩.

So, S1^y S3^y |↑↑↓⟩ = (0 - 0 - 0 + |↓↑⟩)/(-4) = (-1/4)|↓↑⟩.

For |↑↓↑⟩:

S1^+ S3^+ |↑↓↑⟩ = 0 ⊗ 0 = 0,
S1^+ S3^- |↑↓↑⟩ = 0 ⊗ |↑⟩ = 0,
S1^- S3^+ |↑↓↑⟩ = |↓⟩ ⊗ |↑⟩ = |↓↑⟩,
S1^- S3^- |↑↓↑⟩ = |↓⟩ ⊗ |↓⟩ = |↓↓⟩.

So, S1^y S3^y |↑↓↑⟩ = (0 - 0 + |↓↑⟩ + |↓↓⟩)/(-4) = (|↓↑⟩ + |↓↓⟩)/(-4).

For |↓↑↑⟩:

S1^+ S3^+ |↓↑↑⟩ = |↑⟩ ⊗ |↓⟩ = |↑↓⟩,
S1^+ S3^- |↓↑↑⟩ = |↑⟩ ⊗ 0 = 0,
S1^- S3^+ |↓↑↑⟩ = 0 ⊗ |↓⟩ = 0,
S1^- S3^- |↓↑↑⟩ = 0 ⊗ 0 = 0.

Thus, S1^y S3^y |↓↑↑⟩ = (|↑↓⟩ + 0 + 0 + 0)/(-4) = (-1/4)|↑↓⟩.

Putting it together:

S1^y S3^y |ψ⟩ = (1/√3)( (-1/4)|↓↑⟩ + (|↓↑⟩ + |↓↓⟩)/(-4) + (-1/4)|↑↓⟩ ).

Simplify this:

= (1/√3)[ (-1/4)|↓↑⟩ - (|↓↑⟩ + |↓↓⟩)/4 - (1/4)|↑↓⟩ ]

= (1/√3)[ (-1/4 - 1/4)|↓↑⟩ - |↓↓⟩/4 - (1/4)|↑↓⟩ ]

Wait, actually, more precisely:

= (1/√3)[ (-1/4 -1/4)|↓↑⟩ - |↓↓⟩/4 - |↑↓⟩/4 ]

= (1/√3)[ (-1/2)|↓↑⟩ - |↓↓⟩/4 - |↑↓⟩/4 ]

Now, taking the inner product with ψ:

<ψ| S1^y S3^y |ψ> = (1/√3)(⟨↑↑↓| + ⟨↑↓↑| + ⟨↓↑↑| ) * [ (-1/2)|↓↑⟩ - |↓↓⟩/4 - |↑↓⟩/4 ]

= (1/√3) [ (-1/2)(⟨↑↑↓|↓↑⟩) - (⟨↑↑↓|↓↓⟩)/4 - (⟨↑↑↓|↑↓⟩)/4 + (-1/2)(⟨↑↓↑|↓↑⟩)/4 - (⟨↑↓↑|↓↓⟩)/16 - (⟨↑↓↑|↑↓⟩)/16 + (-1/2)(⟨↓↑↑|↓↑⟩)/4 - (⟨↓↑↑|↓↓⟩)/16 - (⟨↓↑↑|↑↓⟩)/16 ]

Wait, this is getting too complicated. Maybe I can note that the only non-zero terms come from when the ket and bra are the same.

Looking for terms where the ket and bra are the same:

- (-1/2)⟨↑↑↓|↓↑⟩ = 0,

Looking for terms where the ket and bra match exactly.

Wait, that's still not correct because the expansion involves more terms.
